\n\n

Current Situation: CAL FIRE’S unified team and the U.S. Forest Service are engaged in a coordinated response to take suppressive action on the August Complex, which has been split into three zones to effectively provide a response for the communities at risk. The complexity of four teams managing one fire resulted in some acres being counted twice. Reconciliation of the acreage calculations puts the current acreage of the August Complex West Zone at 35,398 acres. Resources from across the state of California as well as Montana, Utah, Texas, and New Jersey have been assigned to assist on the August Complex West Zone. The fire remained active today, with isolated torching observed on the southern boundary. It has continued to make\nuphill slope-driven runs when in alignment with topography. A low-pressure system sitting off the west coast will make little progress toward the fire today, resulting in similar weather for tomorrow. Relative humidity will remain fairly low with poor\novernight recoveries for the upper slopes and ridges allowing the fire to remain active through the night.

    NORTH COMPLEX, WEST ZONE\nONLINE STRUCTURE DAMAGE MAP NOW AVAILABLE

    \n\n

    You can find the link to the map here or type in this link, (https://tinyurl.com/y3jmzxnj).\n\n\n

    Current Situation

    \n

    North Zone: The fire was most active today on Red Mountain where winds cast spot fires approximately one half-mile ahead of the slopover that formed overnight. Firefighters focused their efforts to contain them here and in Willow Creek area where additional spotting occurred, and plan to continue picking them up throughout the night. Crews also constructed bulldozer line on both the east and west sides of this slopover to box it in at Oro-Quincy Road.

    \n

    Moving west, firefighters were successful in containing other previous small spot fires and slopovers, while holding the fire along constructed bulldozer lines.

    \n

    To the northeast side of the fire, containment lines are holding well. Firefighters plan to continue patrolling, while also backhauling equipment and initiating road repairs.

    \n

    South Zone: Crews were able to progress with a small amount of firing along the Pacific Crest Trail to Chimney Rock. Just north of Onion Valley winds continue to slowly push the fire northeast into the steep terrain where crews focused on constructing indirect lines to eventually catch it.

    \n

    Along Mooreville Ridge, crews continued to successfully mop up and improve containment lines from Little Grass Valley Reservoir area south to Sly Creek Reservoir, while also constructing and reinforcing bulldozer lines along LaPorte Road.

    \n

    West Zone: Please see CAL FIRE Team 4 updates at: https://www.fire.ca.gov/incidents/2020/8/18/north-complex-fire/ .

    \n

    Structure protection groups are in place surrounding the fire’s perimeter to protect nearby communities in both the North and South Zones.

    \n

    Firing operations in either zone will be dependent on weather conditions tonight

    \n

    Video operational updates and live broadcasts can be viewed on Plumas National Forest’s Facebook page.

    \n\n

    Evacuations and Road Closures

    \n

    Mandatory evacuation orders and advisories are in place for Butte, Plumas, and Yuba Counties. Please check your\nrespective county’s Facebook page for the latest on evacuations and road closures.

    \n\n

    Weather and Air Quality

    \n

    An approaching low pressure system will bring southwest winds with gusts up to 18-25 mph through tomorrow. There will be little temperature or humidity change. Smoke outlook: https://fires.airfire.org/outlooks/EasternSierra or https://www.airnow.gov/

    \n\n

    Forest Closures

    \n

    Due to unprecedented and historic fire conditions throughout the state, the USDA Forest Service Pacific Southwest Region has extended the closure of eighteen National Forests in California, including the Plumas National Forest. https://www.fs.usda.gov/Internet/FSE_DOCUMENTS/fseprd801413.pdf \n

    \n

    Meetings are being broadcast daily through Zoom:

    \n

  • Planning Meeting daily at 7 P.M.: https://usfs.zoomgov.com/j/1600484186 \n

    \n\n\n

    WEST ZONE - *76,900 acres - 20% contained

    \n

    On the afternoon of September 8th, 2020 the North Complex fire entered Butte County with a vengence, driven by extreme winds, heavy dry fuels, and steep terrain. We need to remain vigilant.

    \n

    There was an increase in temperatures today over the fire area due to the smoke layer dissipating but the humidity remained above 20%. The clearing of the smoke also had a negative effect on the fire causing fire activity to increase across the fire area throughout the day.

    \n

    Aircraft, in most cases, had good visibility to be able to fly over the fire assisting firefighters on the ground. A few times smoke did develop over the fire and hampered some aircraft utilization.

    \n

    Firefighters continue to be successful in strengthening several existing containment lines, developing new containment lines and extinguishing several interior hot spots in an attempt to prevent further spread. Firefighters continue to fight to get into those areas of difficult access to make sure those areas of the fire are contained. Because of the dangerous rugged terrain there has been firefighter injuries. Several contingency fire lines are being developed as well.

    \n

    CAL FIRE Damage Assessment Teams continue the documentation of destroyed and damaged structures within the fire area.

    \n

    Total acreage of the North Complex is 273,335 acres @ 34% contained.

    \n

    *77,329 acres included in the 273,335 acre total

    INCIDENT UPDATE 9/15/20 7PM

    \n

    Current situation information from Fresno County:

    \n

    Several changes were made today regarding Fresno County evacuations. Multiple Evacuation Orders were reduced to Evacuation Warnings an multiple Evacuation Warnings were lifted. This change in evacuation status was a result of the excellent work done by fire crews in Jose Basin where the fire pushed over the lines yesterday and threatended structures. New lines were established throughout the day and tested by the wind last night.

    \n

    A tactical firing operation began today in Cherry Valley where the fire backed down to a mid-slope road. This operation is a planned action and will continue over the next operational period. The goal is to remove fuels between the line and the fire’s edge to prevent further spread into Blue Canyon when the wind shifts later this week. The fire is burning actively in the northeast near the South San Joaquin River. Fire continued to back and flank along the east side of the fire. The eastern portion of the fire has burned in a very mosaic pattern with large green islands. These islands of fuel could flare up as weather changes.

    \n

    Tonight, firefighters will continue tactical patrol and line improvement.

    \n\n\n

    Current situation information from Madera County:

    \n

    The Madera County Sheriff’s Office lifted several Evacuation Warnings today. Please see the interactive evacuation map below for evacuation status.

    \n

    The northeast portion of the fire was active again today. Spot fires were observed up to ½ mile ahead of the fire.

    \n

    The fireline is holding well between the San Joaquin drainage and Cascadel Woods. North of Cascadel Woods crews are scouting and improving the 8SO9 Road for use as control line. A secondary road has been located to the west . This road is being assessed for use as control line.

    \n

    A tactical firing operation is being planned for the area around Central Camp. Structures in Central Camp have been prepped and wrapped in the last several days.

    \n

    The fire will be active throughout the evening. Fire will progress primarily to the north and northeast towards Balloon dome, Granite creek, bowler, Portuguese Viewpoint, Globe Rock, and Little Shuteye Peak. Fire will also continue to be active Central Camp, South Fork Bluffs and Whiskey Falls.

    \n\n

    Bullfrog Fire Information

    \n

    The Bullfrog Fire is burning on the Sierra National Forest but is not related to the Creek Fire. An Inciweb page has been established for the fire. To view information open the following link: Sierra National Forest Bullfrog Fire.

    Current Situation: Containment of the Lake Fire has increased to 90% due to the good work of\nfirefighters over the past 24 hours.     The Angeles National Forest has closed all National Forest System lands within the Lake Fire closure area by Order No. 05-01-20-6. No fires of any type including cooking stoves, lanterns, and similar devices which use propane, white gas, or similar fuels are allowed at this time.     VALLEY FIRE PRESS RELEASE

    \n

    Drones (UAV) Prohibited from Fire Area

    \n\n

    Federal, state, and local wildland fire management agencies and the Federal Aviation Administration (FAA) urge members of the public not to fly “Unmanned Aircraft Vehicles (UAV)” or drones over or near wildfires. Unauthorized drone flights pose serious risks to firefighter and public safety and the effectiveness of wildfire suppression operations

    \n

    If an unauthorized drone is detected flying over or near a wildfire, fire managers may have to ground all airtankers, helicopters, and other aerial firefighting aircraft until they can confirm that the drone has left the area and they feel confident that it won’t be coming back. This can cause wildfires to become larger and more costly and to unduly threaten lives, property, and valuable natural and cultural resources.

    \n

    Aerial firefighting aircraft, such as airtankers and helicopters, fly at very low altitudes, typically just a couple of hundred feet above the ground and in the same airspace as drones flown by the public. This creates the potential for a mid-air collision, or a pilot distraction that results in a crash, that could seriously injure or kill aerial and/or ground firefighters.

    \n

    Temporary Flight Restrictions (TFRs) typically put in place during wildfires require manned or unmanned aircraft not involved in wildfire suppression operations to obtain permission to enter specified airspace. The FAA, U.S. Forest Service, U.S. Department of the Interior and other wildland fire management agencies consider drones, including those flown by the public for fun, to be aircraft and therefore subject to TFRs. Members of the public should not fly drones over or near wildfires even if a TFR is not in place because of the potential for accidents and disruption of suppression operations. Individuals who are determined to have interfered with wildfire suppression efforts may be subject to civil penalties of up to $20,000 and potentially\ncriminal prosecution, per California Penal Code Section 402(2). Members of the public who have witnessed, or who have information about an unauthorized drone flight over or near a wildfire, should contact local law enforcement

    \n

    Even though smoke or fire may not be visible, drones should not be operated in or around the wildfire area as firefighting aircraft could still be flying.

    \n

    The U.S. Department of the Interior, in partnership with other federal, state, and local agencies, has developed a wildfire location data-sharing program called “Current Wildland Fires” to inform drone pilots of areas to avoid flying over or near. Additional information is available at https://www.doi.gov/pressreleases/interior-expands-information-sharing-initiative-prevent-drone-incursions

    \n

    Wildland fire management agencies are also using a variety of communication tools to connect with drone pilots. The “If You Fly, We Can’t” safety awareness campaign is designed to keep drone pilots away from airspace used by firefighters. Additional information is available at https://www.nifc.gov/drones/index.html

    CURRENT CONDITIONS: 9/11/20 AM

    \n\n

    Fire crews made great progress last night in the containment of the El Dorado Fire with favorable downslope winds that allowed crews the opportunity to continue fire line construction and strengthening the fire perimeter in all areas around the fire.

    \n\n

    Northern portion of the Yucaipa Ridge: Ground crews will continue working to secure the fire line on the western edge of the fire and making a direct attack with handlines to protect Mountain Home Village. Above Hwy 38, the fire was held at the dozer line and allowed crews to continue building containment line at the fire’s edge. Aircraft will continue providing water and retardant drops today to assist crews on the ground if visibility is good

    \n\n

    The fire continues to progress slowly downslope as it backs down into Forest Falls. The hard work by fire resources over this last week is allowing for a successful defense of structures.

    \n\n

    Fire resources are continuing to prepare structures in Angelus Oaks by increasing defensible space around structures and building indirect hand line.

    \n\n

    On the southern portion of the Yucaipa Ridge (Yucaipa & Oak Glen areas): The fire line is holding with flareups and burning in the interior of the fire perimeter. Fire resources will continue to strengthen the fire line by actively mopping up any hot spots.

    \n \n

    Today the wind will transition back to an up-canyon wind at 8 to 10 mph gusting to 18 mph. The air and fuels remain dry and ready to ignite. Fire remains active with a potential for large growth when in alignment with canyons. Fire resources will continue building containment lines and directly attacking the fire from the air and ground.

    \n\n

    The evacuation warning and order remain in effect for portions of Mentone and Yucaipa. Residents of Angelus Oaks, 7 Oaks, Barton Flats up to Onyx Summit are under an Evacuation order. Please review the Evacuation Warnings and Orders at the end of this update to determine if you live in an evacuated area.

    \n\n

    The San Bernardino County Sheriffs department and the El Dorado Fire Unified Incident Commanders continue the advisory for visitors to consider rescheduling planned visits to the Big Bear area due to fire activity.

    \n\n

    Neighbors, please stay vigilant and check Inciweb, Twitter and Facebook for changes on the #ElDoradoFire. There are physical signboards at the Stater Bros. shopping center in Beaumont at 1430 Beaumont Ave., 1775 east Lugonia Ave. in Redlands near the Starbucks and 11365 Bryant St. Yucaipa in the Stater Bros shopping center.

    \n\n

    The Red Cross temporary evacuation point is at: Redlands East Valley High School, 31000 E. Colton Ave. in Redlands and the Red Cross phone number for evacuation assistance is (442) 242-0946.

    Current Situation: Containment of the Lake Fire has increased to 90% due to the good work of\nfirefighters over the past 24 hours. It has been burning in 100 year-old fuels consisting of Big Cone\nDouglas Fir, Oak, and Gray Pine. The fire is holding northeast of Interstate 5 and south of Highway 138\nin steep and rugged terrain. Control lines have been completed all around the fire’s perimeter. Firefighters are now patrolling the fire\nline to ensure that all lines continue to hold and that there is no heat near the fire’s perimeter.\nFirefighters have been monitoring the fire area for pockets of isolated heat and smoke. When safe to do\nso, firefighters have gone into the interior of the fire area to fully extinguish those hot spots that may\npose a threat of spotting and escaping over containment lines. Helicopters have also been assisting\nground crews in extinguishing these hot spots with water bucket drops. Crews have been able to perform\na significant amount of fire suppression repair around the fire; primarily focusing on blocking off public\naccess to dozers lines, rehabilitating some of these lines and installing a large number of water bars to\nprevent against erosion.     The Angeles National Forest has closed all National Forest System lands within the Lake Fire closure area by Order No. 05-01-20-6. On Saturday, August 1st, the Forest changed its Fire Danger Level from VERY HIGH to EXTREME. Angeles Forest Order No. 0501-20-05 prohibits all campfires within the Angeles National Forest. No fires of any type including cooking stoves, lanterns, and similar devices which use propane, white gas, or similar fuels are allowed at this time.     Current Situation: CAL FIRE’S unified team and the U.S. Forest Service are engaged in a coordinated response to take suppressive action on the August Complex, which has been split into three zones to effectively provide a response for the communities at risk. The complexity of four teams managing one fire resulted in some acres being counted twice. Reconciliation of the acreage calculations puts the current acreage of the August Complex West Zone at 35,398 acres. Resources from across the state of California as well as Montana, Utah, Texas, and New Jersey have been assigned to assist on the August Complex West Zone. The fire remained active today, with isolated torching observed on the southern boundary. It has continued to make\nuphill slope-driven runs when in alignment with topography. A low-pressure system sitting off the west coast will make little progress toward the fire today, resulting in similar weather for tomorrow. Relative humidity will remain fairly low with poor\novernight recoveries for the upper slopes and ridges allowing the fire to remain active through the night.

    NORTH COMPLEX, WEST ZONE\nONLINE STRUCTURE DAMAGE MAP NOW AVAILABLE

    \n\n

    You can find the link to the map here or type in this link, (https://tinyurl.com/y3jmzxnj).\n\n\n

    Current Situation

    \n

    North Zone: The fire was most active today on Red Mountain where winds cast spot fires approximately one half-mile ahead of the slopover that formed overnight. Firefighters focused their efforts to contain them here and in Willow Creek area where additional spotting occurred, and plan to continue picking them up throughout the night. Crews also constructed bulldozer line on both the east and west sides of this slopover to box it in at Oro-Quincy Road.

    \n

    Moving west, firefighters were successful in containing other previous small spot fires and slopovers, while holding the fire along constructed bulldozer lines.

    \n

    To the northeast side of the fire, containment lines are holding well. Firefighters plan to continue patrolling, while also backhauling equipment and initiating road repairs.

    \n

    South Zone: Crews were able to progress with a small amount of firing along the Pacific Crest Trail to Chimney Rock. Just north of Onion Valley winds continue to slowly push the fire northeast into the steep terrain where crews focused on constructing indirect lines to eventually catch it.

    \n

    Along Mooreville Ridge, crews continued to successfully mop up and improve containment lines from Little Grass Valley Reservoir area south to Sly Creek Reservoir, while also constructing and reinforcing bulldozer lines along LaPorte Road.

    \n

    West Zone: Please see CAL FIRE Team 4 updates at: https://www.fire.ca.gov/incidents/2020/8/18/north-complex-fire/ .

    \n

    Structure protection groups are in place surrounding the fire’s perimeter to protect nearby communities in both the North and South Zones.

    \n

    Firing operations in either zone will be dependent on weather conditions tonight

    \n

    Video operational updates and live broadcasts can be viewed on Plumas National Forest’s Facebook page.

    \n\n

    Evacuations and Road Closures

    \n

    Mandatory evacuation orders and advisories are in place for Butte, Plumas, and Yuba Counties. Please check your\nrespective county’s Facebook page for the latest on evacuations and road closures.

    \n\n

    Weather and Air Quality

    \n

    An approaching low pressure system will bring southwest winds with gusts up to 18-25 mph through tomorrow. There will be little temperature or humidity change. Smoke outlook: https://fires.airfire.org/outlooks/EasternSierra or https://www.airnow.gov/

    \n\n

    Forest Closures

    \n

    Due to unprecedented and historic fire conditions throughout the state, the USDA Forest Service Pacific Southwest Region has extended the closure of eighteen National Forests in California, including the Plumas National Forest. https://www.fs.usda.gov/Internet/FSE_DOCUMENTS/fseprd801413.pdf \n

    \n
  • Cooperators Meeting daily at 10 A.M.: https://usfs.zoomgov.com/j/1602646317 \n
  • Planning Meeting daily at 7 P.M.: https://usfs.zoomgov.com/j/1600484186 \n

    WEST ZONE - *76,900 acres - 20% contained

    \n

    On the afternoon of September 8th, 2020 the North Complex fire entered Butte County with a vengence, driven by extreme winds, heavy dry fuels, and steep terrain. We need to remain vigilant.

    \n

    There was an increase in temperatures today over the fire area due to the smoke layer dissipating but the humidity remained above 20%. The clearing of the smoke also had a negative effect on the fire causing fire activity to increase across the fire area throughout the day.

    \n

    Aircraft, in most cases, had good visibility to be able to fly over the fire assisting firefighters on the ground. A few times smoke did develop over the fire and hampered some aircraft utilization.

    \n

    Firefighters continue to be successful in strengthening several existing containment lines, developing new containment lines and extinguishing several interior hot spots in an attempt to prevent further spread. Firefighters continue to fight to get into those areas of difficult access to make sure those areas of the fire are contained. Because of the dangerous rugged terrain there has been firefighter injuries. Several contingency fire lines are being developed as well.

    \n

    CAL FIRE Damage Assessment Teams continue the documentation of destroyed and damaged structures within the fire area.

    \n

    Total acreage of the North Complex is 273,335 acres @ 34% contained.

    \n

    *77,329 acres included in the 273,335 acre total

    BUTTE/TEHAMA/GLENN LIGHTNING COMPLEX TEHAMA/GLENN ZONE INCIDENT UPDATE 09/11/2020 9AM

    \n

    Acreage decreased due to Elkhorn and Hopkins Fires are no longer being accounted for in this Complex. UPDATE 09/10/2020

    \n

    California Interagency Management Incident (CIIMT) Team 5 will assume command\nfrom CAL FIRE Team 4 effective tomorrow morning, 9/9/2020 at 6:00 a.m. CIIMT\nTeam 5 will assume responsibility for the Elkhorn, Hopkins, Vinegar and Willow\nFires. Incident Management Team 1 (Southern Area Blue Team) will remain in\ncommand of the August Complex. CAL FIRE resources will remain to assist the\nincidents with resources. This will be the final incident update from CAL FIRE Team\n4. For all new incident information please visit the following sites.

    \n https://inciweb.nwcg.gov/ then select current disaster info.

    \nTwitter: @ShastaTrinityNF\nFacebook: @ShastaTrinityNF\n

    Tehama Zone has multiple fires burning in the National Forest, including the\nElkhorn Fire at 50,126 acres and 55% containment. Personnel will continue to assist\nwith constructing direct and indirect control lines and provide for structure\ndefense. Personnel are closely monitoring current and expected fire weather\nconditions and will plan and implement evacuation plans as needed. CIIMT Team 5\nwill assume command of the Elkhorn, Hopkins, Vinegar and Willow Fires.

    \n\n\n\n

    Glenn Zonehas multiple fires burning. The August Complex, includes the\nIvory/Doe Fire and the area that was known as the Tatham Fire, has a current total\nacreage of 349,565 acres (total acreage includes both state and federal land; with\n18,981 acres on state lands). Personnel will continue to assist constructing direct\nand indirect control lines and provide for structure defense. Personnel are\nmonitoring weather conditions and will plan and implement evacuations as\nneeded. Incident Management Team 1 (Southern Area Blue Team) will remain in\ncommand of the August Complex.

    \n\n

    The reported acreage of the three fires are as follows:

    \n

    Elkhorn: 50,126 acres, 55% containment

    \n

    August Complex: 349,565 acres, 24% containment

    \n\n\n

    INCIDENT UPDATE 9/15/20 7PM

    \n

    Current situation information from Fresno County:

    \n

    Several changes were made today regarding Fresno County evacuations. Multiple Evacuation Orders were reduced to Evacuation Warnings an multiple Evacuation Warnings were lifted. This change in evacuation status was a result of the excellent work done by fire crews in Jose Basin where the fire pushed over the lines yesterday and threatended structures. New lines were established throughout the day and tested by the wind last night.

    \n

    A tactical firing operation began today in Cherry Valley where the fire backed down to a mid-slope road. This operation is a planned action and will continue over the next operational period. The goal is to remove fuels between the line and the fire’s edge to prevent further spread into Blue Canyon when the wind shifts later this week. The fire is burning actively in the northeast near the South San Joaquin River. Fire continued to back and flank along the east side of the fire. The eastern portion of the fire has burned in a very mosaic pattern with large green islands. These islands of fuel could flare up as weather changes.

    \n

    Tonight, firefighters will continue tactical patrol and line improvement.

    \n\n\n

    Current situation information from Madera County:

    \n

    The Madera County Sheriff’s Office lifted several Evacuation Warnings today. Please see the interactive evacuation map below for evacuation status.

    \n

    The northeast portion of the fire was active again today. Spot fires were observed up to ½ mile ahead of the fire.

    \n

    The fireline is holding well between the San Joaquin drainage and Cascadel Woods. North of Cascadel Woods crews are scouting and improving the 8SO9 Road for use as control line. A secondary road has been located to the west . This road is being assessed for use as control line.

    \n

    A tactical firing operation is being planned for the area around Central Camp. Structures in Central Camp have been prepped and wrapped in the last several days.

    \n

    The fire will be active throughout the evening. Fire will progress primarily to the north and northeast towards Balloon dome, Granite creek, bowler, Portuguese Viewpoint, Globe Rock, and Little Shuteye Peak. Fire will also continue to be active Central Camp, South Fork Bluffs and Whiskey Falls.

    \n\n

    Bullfrog Fire Information

    \n

    The Bullfrog Fire is burning on the Sierra National Forest but is not related to the Creek Fire. An Inciweb page has been established for the fire. To view information open the following link: Sierra National Forest Bullfrog Fire.

    \n\n

    Animal Evacuation Centers:

    \n

    Fresno County

    \n

    Small animals – Clovis North 2770 East International Ave.

    \n

    Large animals – The Fresno Fairgrounds (1121 S Chance Ave, Fresno, CA 93702) is set up to receive evacuated animals, but please contact the Central California Animal Disaster Team (1-888-402-2238) to finalize arrangements so you can be received at o Fairgrounds.

    \n

    Small animals – Oakhurst Community Center 39800 Road 425B Oakhurst, CA

    CURRENT CONDITIONS: 9/11/20 AM

    \n\n

    Fire crews made great progress last night in the containment of the El Dorado Fire with favorable downslope winds that allowed crews the opportunity to continue fire line construction and strengthening the fire perimeter in all areas around the fire.

    \n\n

    Northern portion of the Yucaipa Ridge: Ground crews will continue working to secure the fire line on the western edge of the fire and making a direct attack with handlines to protect Mountain Home Village. Above Hwy 38, the fire was held at the dozer line and allowed crews to continue building containment line at the fire’s edge. Aircraft will continue providing water and retardant drops today to assist crews on the ground if visibility is good

    \n\n

    The fire continues to progress slowly downslope as it backs down into Forest Falls. The hard work by fire resources over this last week is allowing for a successful defense of structures.

    \n\n

    Fire resources are continuing to prepare structures in Angelus Oaks by increasing defensible space around structures and building indirect hand line.

    \n\n

    On the southern portion of the Yucaipa Ridge (Yucaipa & Oak Glen areas): The fire line is holding with flareups and burning in the interior of the fire perimeter. Fire resources will continue to strengthen the fire line by actively mopping up any hot spots.

    \n \n

    Today the wind will transition back to an up-canyon wind at 8 to 10 mph gusting to 18 mph. The air and fuels remain dry and ready to ignite. Fire remains active with a potential for large growth when in alignment with canyons. Fire resources will continue building containment lines and directly attacking the fire from the air and ground.

    \n\n

    The evacuation warning and order remain in effect for portions of Mentone and Yucaipa. Residents of Angelus Oaks, 7 Oaks, Barton Flats up to Onyx Summit are under an Evacuation order. Please review the Evacuation Warnings and Orders at the end of this update to determine if you live in an evacuated area.

    \n\n

    The San Bernardino County Sheriffs department and the El Dorado Fire Unified Incident Commanders continue the advisory for visitors to consider rescheduling planned visits to the Big Bear area due to fire activity.

    \n\n

    Neighbors, please stay vigilant and check Inciweb, Twitter and Facebook for changes on the #ElDoradoFire. There are physical signboards at the Stater Bros. shopping center in Beaumont at 1430 Beaumont Ave., 1775 east Lugonia Ave. in Redlands near the Starbucks and 11365 Bryant St. Yucaipa in the Stater Bros shopping center.

    \n\n

    The Red Cross temporary evacuation point is at: Redlands East Valley High School, 31000 E. Colton Ave. in Redlands and the Red Cross phone number for evacuation assistance is (442) 242-0946.

    VALLEY FIRE PRESS RELEASE

    \n

    Drones (UAV) Prohibited from Fire Area

    \n\n

    Federal, state, and local wildland fire management agencies and the Federal Aviation Administration (FAA) urge members of the public not to fly “Unmanned Aircraft Vehicles (UAV)” or drones over or near wildfires. Unauthorized drone flights pose serious risks to firefighter and public safety and the effectiveness of wildfire suppression operations

    \n

    If an unauthorized drone is detected flying over or near a wildfire, fire managers may have to ground all airtankers, helicopters, and other aerial firefighting aircraft until they can confirm that the drone has left the area and they feel confident that it won’t be coming back. This can cause wildfires to become larger and more costly and to unduly threaten lives, property, and valuable natural and cultural resources.

    \n

    Aerial firefighting aircraft, such as airtankers and helicopters, fly at very low altitudes, typically just a couple of hundred feet above the ground and in the same airspace as drones flown by the public. This creates the potential for a mid-air collision, or a pilot distraction that results in a crash, that could seriously injure or kill aerial and/or ground firefighters.

    \n

    Temporary Flight Restrictions (TFRs) typically put in place during wildfires require manned or unmanned aircraft not involved in wildfire suppression operations to obtain permission to enter specified airspace. The FAA, U.S. Forest Service, U.S. Department of the Interior and other wildland fire management agencies consider drones, including those flown by the public for fun, to be aircraft and therefore subject to TFRs. Members of the public should not fly drones over or near wildfires even if a TFR is not in place because of the potential for accidents and disruption of suppression operations. Individuals who are determined to have interfered with wildfire suppression efforts may be subject to civil penalties of up to $20,000 and potentially\ncriminal prosecution, per California Penal Code Section 402(2). Members of the public who have witnessed, or who have information about an unauthorized drone flight over or near a wildfire, should contact local law enforcement

    \n

    Even though smoke or fire may not be visible, drones should not be operated in or around the wildfire area as firefighting aircraft could still be flying.

    \n

    The U.S. Department of the Interior, in partnership with other federal, state, and local agencies, has developed a wildfire location data-sharing program called “Current Wildland Fires” to inform drone pilots of areas to avoid flying over or near. Additional information is available at https://www.doi.gov/pressreleases/interior-expands-information-sharing-initiative-prevent-drone-incursions

    \n

    Wildland fire management agencies are also using a variety of communication tools to connect with drone pilots. The “If You Fly, We Can’t” safety awareness campaign is designed to keep drone pilots away from airspace used by firefighters. Additional information is available at https://www.nifc.gov/drones/index.html
